text-align: left; background-color: #f9ffbc;">Transcriptions</th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Standard Mandarin</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanyu_Pinyin" title="Hanyu Pinyin">Hanyu Pinyin</a></th><td><span lang="zh-Latn" style="font-style:normal" title="Chinese-language romanization">Běijīng Guóān</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Spelling_in_Gwoyeu_Romatzyh" title="Spelling in Gwoyeu Romatzyh">Gwoyeu Romatzyh</a></th><td><span lang="zh-Latn" style="font-style:normal" title="Chinese-language romanization">Beeijing Gwoan</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles" title="Wade–Giles">Wade–Giles</a></th><td><span lang="zh-Latn" style="font-style:normal" title="Chinese-language romanization">Peich'ing Kuoan</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Mandarin" title="Help:IPA/Mandarin">IPA</a></th><td><span lang="zh-Latn" style="font-style:normal" title="Chinese-language romanization"><span class="IPA" style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Mandarin" title="Help:IPA/Mandarin">[pèitɕíŋ kwǒˈán]</a></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Beijing Sinobo Guoan F.C.</b> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">北京中赫国安</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Běijīng Zhōnghè Guó'ān</span></i>) is a professional Chinese <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club that currently participates in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a> under licence from the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Football_Association" title="Chinese Football Association">Chinese Football Association</a> (CFA). The team is based in the <a href="/wiki/Chaoyang_District,_Beijing" title="Chaoyang District, Beijing">Chaoyang District</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> and their home stadium is the <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Stadium" title="Workers' Stadium">Workers' Stadium</a> with a seating capacity of 66,161. Their shareholders are the real estate company Sinobo Group (64%) and <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Limited" title="CITIC Limited">CITIC Limited</a> (36%) of <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Group" title="CITIC Group">CITIC Group</a>, a state-owned enterprise of China. Beijing Guoan F.C. was founded as a professional team by <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Guoan_Group" title="CITIC Guoan Group">CITIC Guoan Group</a>, which was a subsidiary of CITIC Group until 2014. The club is one of the four teams to never have been relegated from the league since its debut in 2004. 
</p><p>The club's predecessor was called <b>Beijing Football Club</b> and they predominantly played in the top tier, where they won several domestic league and cup titles. On December 29, 1992 the club was recognized to become a completely professional football club making them one of the founding members of the first fully professional top tier league in China. Since then they have gone on to win their first ever professional league title in the <a href="/wiki/2009_Chinese_Super_League" title="2009 Chinese Super League">2009 league season</a> as well as the 1996, 1997, 2003 and 2018 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_FA_Cup" title="Chinese FA Cup">Chinese FA Cup</a>.
</p><p>According to <i>Forbes</i>, Guoan was the second most valuable football team in China, with a team value of US$167 million, and an estimated revenue of US$30 million in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> According to the disclosure of <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Limited" title="CITIC Limited">CITIC Pacific</a>, the club revenue was CN¥244 million in 2013 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2015 season, the sponsorship from <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Securities" title="CITIC Securities">CITIC Securities</a> was CN¥25 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_club_era">Early club era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early club era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The club's first incarnation came in 1951 when the local government sports body decided to take part in China's first fully nationalized national football league tournament and decided to form a football team with the best players from <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a> to create the North China team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The team name was taken from the football team in the 1910 multi-sport event <a href="/wiki/National_Games_of_China" title="National Games of China">Chinese National Games</a> that also represented the same regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The team ended up finishing fourth in their debut season and with the football league gradually expanding, the players from Beijing and Tianjin were allowed to separate and the local Beijing government sports body was allowed to reform the club as Beijing Football Club in 1955. The club would make its debut appearance in the 1956 season and wore an all white home kit and all red away strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23yy.com_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-23yy.com-6">[6]</a></sup> In the 1956 campaign the club were also allowed to enter their youth team called Beijing Youth B who actually went on to win the league title while Beijing came sixth that season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_1956_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-China_1956-7">[7]</a></sup> The club would strengthen their hold on the following seasons when they went out and won the 1957 as well as the 1958 league titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> With these results, the club would become a major force within Chinese football, and with the club's youth team still participating within the top tier, there was a constant supply of players coming into the team to fight for places. Being China's capital city and for their success on the field, the club would become a feeder team for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/China_PR_national_football_team" title="China PR national football team">Chinese national team</a>. This often saw the club unable to complete a full championship schedule and the youth team were often used to represent the club, which did little to diminish Beijing football and actually resulted in the youth team to win the 1963 championship for the second time, showing the strength in depth of the region of Beijing football until 1966 when the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a> halted football within the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf_1963_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf_1963-9">[9]</a></sup> When football returned to the China, Beijing would win the 1973 league title in the newly re-established footballing league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> While Beijing once again re-established themselves as major title contenders, they didn't win any major titles until 1982 league title, which was then followed by the 1984 league title and 1985 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_FA_Cup" title="Chinese FA Cup">Chinese FA Cup</a> title. After this period, the club would start to decline in their performances and were relegated for the first time in their history at the end of the 1988 season, however, their time within the second tier was short lived and they won the division title and promotion to the first tier at the end of the 1990 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In total, Beijing would have won the league title five times during the old Chinese National Football League era before the club was given full professionalism in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-List_of_Champions_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-List_of_Champions-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professionalism">Professionalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Professionalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beijing Guoan was formed on December 31, 1992, as a result of the Chinese football reform, which was the Chinese Football Association looking to professionalize the whole of the Chinese football league. The club was set up by the <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Guoan_Group" title="CITIC Guoan Group">CITIC Guoan</a> of <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Group" title="CITIC Group">CITIC Group</a> a state-owned enterprise of China and the Beijing Municipal Sports Committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hist_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-hist-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The club would take part in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jia-A_League_1994" title="Chinese Jia-A League 1994">1994 Chinese Jia-A League</a> season, making them a founding member of the first fully professional top tier league in China and changed their home colors to green to symbolize the change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23yy.com_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-23yy.com-6">[6]</a></sup> In their first professional season Beijing finished in a disappointing eighth out of twelve teams and the manager <a href="/wiki/Tang_Pengju" title="Tang Pengju">Tang Pengju</a> was relieved of his duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The club would bring in <a href="/wiki/Jin_Zhiyang" title="Jin Zhiyang">Jin Zhiyang</a> to manage them the following season and results under his reign improved enough for them to finish the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jia-A_League_1995" title="Chinese Jia-A League 1995">1995 campaign</a> in the runners-up position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The following season Jin Zhiyang lead Beijing to their first professional trophy when he beat <a href="/wiki/Shandong_Luneng_Taishan_F.C." title="Shandong Luneng Taishan F.C.">Jinan Taishan Jiangjun</a> 4–1 to lift the 1996 Chinese FA Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Jin Zhiyang was able to retain the Cup the following year with a 2–1 victory against <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Greenland_Shenhua_F.C." title="Shanghai Greenland Shenhua F.C.">Shanghai Shenhua</a>, which impressed the Chinese FA who lured him away from Beijing when they offered him a position with the Chinese national team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The assistant coach <a href="/wiki/Shen_Xiangfu" title="Shen Xiangfu">Shen Xiangfu</a> stepped into the managerial role and in his debut season he guided the club to third within the league, however in his second season the team slid down to sixth and he left the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_influences">Foreign influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Foreign influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Serbian <a href="/wiki/Milovan_%C4%90ori%C4%87" title="Milovan Đorić">Milovan Đorić</a> would be Beijing's first foray with a foreign manager when he joined the club at the start of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jia-A_League_2000" title="Chinese Jia-A League 2000">2000 league season</a>. His reign was exceptionally short-lived after he lost his first three games of the season before he was replaced with native coach <a href="/wiki/Wei_Kexing" title="Wei Kexing">Wei Kexing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> At the start of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jia-A_League_2002" title="Chinese Jia-A League 2002">2002 league season</a> Beijing hired their second foreign manager in <a href="/wiki/Ljupko_Petrovi%C4%87" title="Ljupko Petrović">Ljupko Petrović</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Foreign influences would continue when in 2003, the club signed a three-year endorsement contract with jointly owned South Korean company <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Hyundai" title="Beijing Hyundai">Beijing Hyundai</a>, which resulted in the club changing its name to Beijing Hyundai to accommodate this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In 2005 Spanish football club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> went into negotiations with Beijing on a football develop project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> At the start of the 2007 league season two time Chinese FA Cup winner with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chongqing_Lifan_F.C." title="Chongqing Lifan F.C.">Chongqing Lifan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qingdao_Jonoon_F.C." title="Qingdao Jonoon F.C.">Qingdao Beilaite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Jang-soo" title="Lee Jang-soo">Lee Jang-soo</a> was hired as the teams manager. The South Korean manager in his debut season guided the club to second within the league. By the <a href="/wiki/2009_Chinese_Super_League" title="2009 Chinese Super League">2009 league season</a> the club had returned to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Workers_Stadium" title="Workers Stadium">Workers Stadium</a> after it had been renovation for the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> and under Lee Jang-soo's helm it looked as if the club would be winning its first professional league title until a 2–0 defeat from <a href="/wiki/Changchun_Yatai_F.C." title="Changchun Yatai F.C.">Changchun Yatai</a> on September 15, 2009 saw the club slip to third and Lee Jang-soo was unscrupulously fired with seven games remaining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Former Beijing player <a href="/wiki/Hong_Yuanshuo" title="Hong Yuanshuo">Hong Yuanshuo</a> was immediately brought into the team and on the final day of the season Beijing thrashed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hangzhou_Greentown_F.C." title="Hangzhou Greentown F.C.">Hangzhou Greentown</a> 4–0 to clinch the 2009 league championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite founded by <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Guoan_Group" title="CITIC Guoan Group">CITIC Guoan Group</a>, the stake of the football club was held by another subsidiary CITIC Corp., Ltd. (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">中国中信股份有限公司</span>) of <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Group" title="CITIC Group">CITIC Group</a>, a Beijing incorporated SPV for a possible listing in the mainland China since 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> (CITIC Group invited other investors to purchase the new share of CITIC Guoan Group in 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> making the company no longer a subsidiary of CITIC Group) In 2014, CITIC Group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Backdoor_listing" title="Backdoor listing">backdoor listing</a> most of their assets to their Hong Kong based subsidiary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CITIC_Pacific" title="CITIC Pacific">CITIC Pacific</a> (renaming to <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Limited" title="CITIC Limited">CITIC Limited</a>) including the entire share capital of "CITIC Corp.", thus the stake of the football club was indirectly floated in a stock exchange.
</p><p>On 27 December 2016 real estate company <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sinobo_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sinobo Group (page does not exist)">Sinobo Group</a> participated the capital increase of the club for a reported 64% stake which was finalised on 10 January 2017, making them the largest shareholder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> According to Chinese Government database, the share capital of the club had increase from <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">CN¥</a>75 million to CN¥208.33 million, making Sinobo Group would owned 64.00% stake with CN¥133.33 million par value and undisclosed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Share_premium" title="Share premium">share premium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-database_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-database-30">[30]</a></sup> The club was also renamed to <b>Beijing Sinobo Guoan F.C. Co., Ltd.</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-database_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-database-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_history">Name history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Name history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>1956: <b>Beijing Physical Education Normal University</b> 北京体院队<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_1956_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-China_1956-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
<li>1957–1960: <b>Beijing</b> 北京队</li>
<li>1961–1964: <b>Beijing Youth</b> 北京青年队<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsssf_1963_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf_1963-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li>1965–1990: <b>Beijing</b> 北京队</li>
<li>1991: <b>Beijing Shenzhou</b> 北京神州队<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>1992: <b>Beijing</b> 北京队</li>
<li>1993–2002: <b>Beijing Guoan</b> 北京国安队<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weltfussballarchiv_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-weltfussballarchiv-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>2003–2005: <b>Beijing Hyundai</b> 北京现代队<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weltfussballarchiv_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-weltfussballarchiv-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>2006–2015: <b>Beijing Guoan</b> 北京国安队</li>
<li>2016: <b>Beijing Guoan LeEco</b> 北京国安乐视队<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>2017–: <b>Beijing Sinobo Guoan</b> 北京中赫国安队</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_stadiums">Home stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Home stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Three stadiums has been used as the home court of Beijing Guoan since 1994: <a href="/wiki/Xiannongtan_Stadium" title="Xiannongtan Stadium">Xiannongtan Stadium</a> (1994–95), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Worker%27s_Stadium" title="Worker's Stadium">Worker's Stadium</a> (1996–05, 2009–present) and <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Fengtai_Stadium" title="Beijing Fengtai Stadium">Beijing Fengtai Stadium</a> (2006–08).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kits_and_crest">Kits and crest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Kits and crest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beijing_Guoan_F.C." title="Beijing Guoan F.C.">Beijing Guoan F.C.</a>'s main color is green.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Beijing Guoan's fiercest and oldest rivalry is against <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Greenland_Shenhua_F.C." title="Shanghai Greenland Shenhua F.C.">Shanghai Shenhua</a> and is often referred to as the China Derby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The rivalry with Shenhua is viewed as a manifestation of the rivalry that exist between the cities on which is the most import towards the country, as one is the center of government while the other is the <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">Financial centre</a> of modern commerce within China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> With each club being able to claim to having an extensive history spanning successful periods, direct competition for silverware, however rarely coincided until the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jia-A_League_1997" title="Chinese Jia-A League 1997">1997 league season</a>. With Shenhua having won the 1995 league title and Beijing having won the 1996 Chinese FA Cup both teams looked as if they had the pedigree to win silverware that season and on July 20, 1997 in a vital league game, Beijing thrashed Shenhua 9–1 at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Workers_Stadium" title="Workers Stadium">Workers Stadium</a> in Beijing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> It would be Beijing's largest  victory and Shenhua's greatest defeat ever recorded. Soon after that event both teams would meet again in the 1997 FA Cup final, which saw Beijing win the cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Jing-Jin derby is a local rivalry between Beijing Guoan and neighboring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tianjin_Teda_F.C." title="Tianjin Teda F.C.">Tianjin Teda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Both teams can trace their histories to the North China team before it split to form the Beijing Football Club and Tianjin Football Club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_1956_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-China_1956-7">[7]</a></sup> Since then both clubs have predominantly remained within the top tier of Chinese football providing a constant rivalry fixture, which has led to intense matches that have spilled out away from the stadiums and onto the streets that have led to property destruction as well as further intensifying their relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_squad">Current squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Current squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retired_numbers_in_football_(soccer)" title="Retired numbers in football (soccer)">Retired numbers in football</a></div>
<p><big><b>12</b></big> – <a href="/wiki/12th_man_(football)" title="12th man (football)">Club Supporters (the 12th Man)</a> retired in Jan 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p><big><b>13</b></big>  retired for the legend, <a href="/wiki/Xu_Yunlong" title="Xu Yunlong">Xu Yunlong</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_team_2">First team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: First team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All-time honours list including semi-professional Beijing period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-List_of_Champions_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-List_of_Champions-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a></b></li></ul>
<dl><dd><b>Winners</b>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League_2009" title="Chinese Super League 2009">2009</a></dd>
<dd><i>Runners-up</i> (3): 2007, 2011, 2014</dd></dl>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jia-A_League" title="Chinese Jia-A League">Chinese Jia-A League</a></b></li></ul>
<dl><dd>Winners (5): 1957, 1958, 1973, 1982, 1984</dd></dl>

<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_2"><b><a href="#ref_2">^2</a></b></span>  In final group stage.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_3"><b><a href="#ref_3">^3</a></b></span>  Unable to complete full season, Youth team representing region.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_4"><b><a href="#ref_4">^4</a></b></span>  Did not play for position.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_5"><b><a href="#ref_5">^5</a></b></span>  Deducted one point.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_6"><b><a href="#ref_6">^6</a></b></span>  In the northern league.</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wins">Wins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Wins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>Biggest home win overall:</b> 9–1 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Shenhua" title="Shanghai Shenhua">Shanghai Shenhua</a> July 20, 1997 – Jia-A League)</li>
<li><b>Biggest away win overall:</b> 8–0 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Radiant" title="New Radiant">New Radiant</a> Aug 29, 1997 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Cup_Winners_Cup" title="Asian Cup Winners Cup">Asian Cup Winners Cup</a>)</li>
<li><b>Biggest home win in the league:</b> 9–1 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Shenhua" title="Shanghai Shenhua">Shanghai Shenhua</a> July 20, 1997 – Jia-A League)</li>
<li><b>Biggest away win in the league:</b> 6–1 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shandong_Luneng" title="Shandong Luneng">Shandong Luneng</a> Aug 8, 2007 – <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a>)</li>
<li><b>Biggest home win in all Asian competitions:</b> 4–0 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salgaocar_SC_Goa" title="Salgaocar SC Goa">Salgaocar SC Goa</a> Oct 3, 1998 – Asian Cup Winners Cup) <br/> 4–0 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Radiant" title="New Radiant">New Radiant</a> Aug 27, 1997 – Asian Cup Winners Cup)</li>
<li><b>Biggest away win in all Asian competitions:</b> 8–0 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Radiant" title="New Radiant">New Radiant</a> Aug 29, 1997 – Asian Cup Winners Cup)</li>
<li><b>Biggest home win in FA Cup:</b> 6–0 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qingdao_Zhongneng" title="Qingdao Zhongneng">Qingdao Zhongneng</a> July 18, 2012)</li>
<li><b>Biggest away win in FA Cup:</b> 5–0 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayi_FC" title="Bayi FC">Bayi FC</a> Sept 20, 1997)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defeats">Defeats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Defeats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>Biggest away defeat overall:</b> 0–5 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shandong_Luneng" title="Shandong Luneng">Shandong Luneng</a> (a) June 2, 2004 – <a href="/wiki/Chinese_FA_Cup" title="Chinese FA Cup">FA Cup</a>) <br/> 0–5 (<a href="/wiki/Suwon_Samsung_Bluewings" title="Suwon Samsung Bluewings">Suwon Samsung Bluewings</a> April 10, 1998 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Cup_Winners_Cup" title="Asian Cup Winners Cup">Asian Cup Winners Cup</a>)</li>
<li><b>Biggest away defeat in the league:</b> 1–5 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dalian_Shide" title="Dalian Shide">Dalian Wanda</a> July 13, 1997 – Jia A League)</li>
<li><b>Biggest home defeat overall:</b> 0–4 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Changchun_Yatai" title="Changchun Yatai">Changchun Yatai</a> Sept 29, 2012 – <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a>)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Streaks">Streaks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Sinobo_Guoan_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Streaks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>Consecutive league wins:</b> 7 (from Aug 31, 2014 to Oct 26, 2014)</li>
<li><b>Consecutive league matches unbeaten:</b> 18 (Sept 28, 2008, Round 18 – April 17, 2009, Round 5), (April 17, 2011, Round 3 – Aug 17, 2011, Round 21)</li>
<li><b>Consecutive league home matches unbeaten:</b> 29 (Sept 29, 1996 – April 4, 1999)</li></ul>
